ACTION EQUINES SERVICES
Action Required: None, FYI
1. Forwarded herewith for Headquarters information and
files is an Agent Service Record on LIRING-3.
2. As Addressees are aware. Wallace P. ROWTON ranrured
and formerly handled LIRING-3 for the Mexico City Station.
Prior to ROWTON's PCS departure from Mexico City in July 1969,
it was deciced, after some discussion, to effect the removal of
the U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S.
LIRING-3 apparently
had been well "burned" with the Cubans, he seemed to have maintained
good contacts with members of the Rebel Armed Forces (FAR) of
Guatemala. In addition, in May and June of this year, he had
been the U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S. U.S.
interest. It was therefore decided to run LIRING-3 on a trial
basis to determine whether he could be used effectively against
Central American revolutionary targets, despite his problems with
the Cubans.
3. ROWTON introduced Leonard S. TORMET, in alias, to LIRING-3
on 1 July 1969. Although ROWTON had represented himself to LIRING-3
as a Greek businessman, it was decided that it would be preferable
to "clear the air" somewhat with LIRING-3, at least by making it

LIRING/MYERAI/Tumberto COOZALEZ Vega
ACTION HOURS: EUREAS
ACTION REQUIRED: See paragraph 2
REPERENCE
: BEMA-36114, 27 December 1968
1. Endgurter's files contain the following information on a Emberto
OCEALEZ and Emberto OCEALZE Vega who is probably identical with the
OCEALEZ described by LIRING/3 in reference.
a. In September 1954 one Umberto COOZALEZ, in company with other
exiles, was deported from Guatemala to Panama. On 9 September this
erile group arrived in Panama on board an Argentine military aircraft.
It was further reported that on 10 September, this same group
departed for Argentina via OCAUQUIL, Lima, and Santiago. COOZALEZ,
described as a Dataselman national, utilized safe conduct pass #1292
or #1295, with listed his occupation as being a railroad worker
and 10 September 1954.
17 September 1954
b. In early May 1957 one Umberto COOZALEZ Tega was reported as
being a member of the Aliar'a de la Juventad Domenzatica de
Oatemala. (AJUG), a Communist youth group. This group was active
in the United States. The American Tobacco Company, the being
directed against the Oatemala Government. OCEALEZ was further
identified as an individual who had previously taken asylum in the
Argentina Embassy, had a known Communist background, and was presently
employed as a salesman for the MLOL Company in Guatemala City.
(Osuree: 102-965, 2 May 1957, ESCOUN/2 from ESCURO/10)
c. On 25 April 1959 one Nuberto OCEALEZ Vega attended a meeting
at which plans for May by celebrations were discussed. This same
report contained two Field Comment that OCEALEZ was a member of
the ROP. (Source: 102-259, 28 April 1959)
/continued/

Orig. and 1 - cos, Mexico City

Evelope addressÃ© to Solor Carlos Gurado
Eurifico Cendres L.6
Pachuca y Vericruz
Mexico, 27
No returns address
Sender's initials: M.3.
Postmarked 16 December, 1968, Guatemala.
Cuszenala, December, 1968.
Dear Carlos:
Excuse as for not having replied to yours of 12 November until today,
but the affairs of the "patojos" keep ce on the go and besides : have
been sick and upset and I keep forgetting everything. That's the reason
I haven't put a date on this letter; you won't believe it but I write
two letters that never get off, but it's true. We hope that you are as
well as ever with your family.
I have to tell you that the "hobre de la bicicleta" wrote ne last week
and that I am a little peeved at in because he speaks ill of you. You
shouic move cautiously, but don't think that it's a problem with us -
we don't believe it. We feel that it's from fear. I lost his address
and for that reason don't intend to write to him.
"El vigotudo" sends you regards; La reza a warn ecrase; la chiquita
a kiss; Elsa.FelisaCari,Varia Elens,Guri and the "patojos" many regares
and embraces for the Chirsmas holidays. The "patojos" are still in the
"pina" so they couldn't come. We'll see whether they can be with us the
24th; if not we'11 have to go there to be with them. In any case I'11 let
you know when they. come here.
So long with many best wishes and congratulations to you and your wife and
children. Excuse the long and boring letter.
So long Carlos,
/s/ Karta

CONINUATION OF
DISPARCH
SECRET/RYBET
HOMA - 36185
2. Operations in PERUMEN and Against Visiting PERUKEN
Officials:
A. LIGILE-1: LIGILE-1 came to Mexico on
19 October and returned to PERUMEN on 1 November,
but he did not contact the Station. (See EXICO
CITY-7874.)
B. LICARD-1: LECARD-1 returned from his TDY
to Madrid in October. His mission was unsuccessful.
The Jndrid Station provided detailed reports on
this operation.
C. LISAGA-1: LISAGA-1 returned to Mexico on
25 November 1968. He remained in Mexico to receive
special training and to undergo debriefing by a
Headquarters TDYer until 9 December, when he returned
to PERUMEN.
Subject of MEXICO CITY-6286: LILADIB-1
finished his debriefing of Subject during this period.
(See HUMA-SOIR )
E. HAGLIDER-1: HAGLIDER-1 did not return to
Mexico during this period.
F. YNAIT-2: YUWAIT-2 did not return to Mexico
during this period.
G. Subject of MEXICO CITY-7595: Subject
defected to the Mexicans during the Olympics. The
Station arranged for a press conference through
LITAMIL-3. LITAMIL-3's debriefing revealed that
Subject did not have any intelligence of value.
(See also LITAIL-3's debriefing)
A. LITAILLOV-1: ANWILLOV-1 arrived in Mexico
on 22 November and returned to PRUMEN on 2 December.
FRADYER could not meet him as he was at Headquarters
on TDY. (See MEXICO CITY-8215 and -8335.)
3. Active Leads to Prospects in PBRUMEN:
A. Subject of MEXICO CITY-5442: LICORET-2
received a call from Subject on 24 November asking
him to take care of two friends who were visiting
Mexico from PRUMEN. During the same call, Subject
indicated he would be coming to Mexico City soon on
vacation and would notify LICORET-2 of the exact
date and details.
E. ANICARUS-1: After enlisting the cooperation
of AMICARUS-3 in Veracruz, the Station is awaiting
the meeting of the ICAURUS-1, scheduled to transit!
Mexico City from PRUMEN, to re-evised fish contact
between the two and have AMICARUS-3 develop AMICARUS-1.
(See MEXICO CITY-8136, et cetera.)
C. ANCAJOLE-2: Per MEXICO CITY-7451 and -7453,
AMCJOLE-1 was scheduled to visit MEXICO from PRUMEN.
However, his father at the last minute reportedly
"blocked" his departure. (See also MEXICO CITY-7574
and -7622.)

28 November, 1968
Subject:
LIRING/3 Report of Meeting with LIRING/9.
1. LIRING/3 reported to Rowton at 0915 on 27/11/65 that he had met with
LIRING/9 at the LIRING establishment from about 1745 until 1900 on 26/11/63.
He stated that he gave LIRING/9 his written report on his recent experiences
in Guatemala and the conclusions be drew from talking with FAR members there.
L/3 also stated that he did his best to assure L/9 that, aithough he sympathized
with the laments of the LeÃ³n Parrios brothers, he was really on the PRUNKEN
side and offered to do all he could to assist theILRINGa in their attempts to
assist the revolutionary forces. The following is Rowton's reconstruction of
the conversation, based on LIRING/3's report:
L/3: "I'm sorry to be late, but I had to finish the report."
L/9: "Alright. I've been waiting here at the gate so there wouldn't
be any further delay. Let's go to my office so we can talk pri-
tely."
Upon entering office, L/9 removes jacket and offers L/3 a seat in the
office.
L/3: "Well, here's my report. I must apologize that it's in rough draft
form. I had to write it rather hurriedly when my wife was not around.
It's really just a series of badly organized thoughts and ideas but
I'll be glad to explain. There's a great deal more, of course, that
I could explain on the subject. Do you wish me to read it?"
L/9: "No, that's alright.
L/9 glances through the report and continues:
"I'11 read it carefully later. I really didn't expect such a long
report. I appreciate it. In the meantime, how are you dobing in your
personal affairs??
L/3: "well, as I told you last time, I'm very much up in the air at the
moment. My exposition has started but is not going as well as can be
expected - as well as I had hoped. You know, these things have their
up's and down's. I'11 sell some things, at least to cover my current
expenses, but I'11 really have to get better organized financially
in the near future. The first problem that I'm really worried about
is my wife, and I frankly feel that I must appeal to you for help.
L/9: "Of course. Well, what is the problem?"
L/3: "As you know, some time ago my wife and I had a series of unpleasant
situations that almost led to a separation.
L/9: "Is that right! "as it that serious?" "anything political?"
L/3: " No, abacutely not. It was purely a domestic misunderstanding. Now
I
il
I feel that I must be very frank with you. I was probably responsible

from that quarter. However, I feel that I should explain that I have
an obligation to my wife for all that she did not me while I was in
jail with no help from anyone, as you well know."
L/9: "Yes, it was difficult for her."
L/3: "You see, my wife is a sincere revolutionary, but she really doesn't
want anv part of the activity that
many others, including my former cell-mate and his famous uncle, who
talk a great revolution, but fall apart when the chips are down."
L/9: "Yes, we know plenty of those types."
L/3: "Well, anyway, my wife wouldn't approve of my reinvolvement and keeps
pressing me to take a "respectable" job which she knows I could obtain
through my friends. that I really want to do is to somehow calm her down
and arrange things so that she won't have any idea of my political plans.
As you know her father is very ill in New York, and she is anxious to
see him before he dies. I can arrange an exposition in Montreal and then
ask the father to come up to see us there. That would get around the
problem of a U.S. visa, which I'a sure neither of us could get."
L/9: "No. I'm sure you couldn't."
L/3: "The only problem is transporta ion. Air passage is too expensive and
unfortunately there are no boats going from here. They all stop at New
Tork. Don't you have regular ship traffic to Montreal, so that we could
go that way?"
L/9: "Yes we do. I'm sure that could be arranged. I see no problem."
L/3: "We could then kill two birds with one stone, by stopping off at the
FARMEN capital enroute."
L/9: "Yes, there's really no problem."
L/9: "I hope you understand my problem. I'm in a very serious way financially
at the moment, and couldn't possibly solve this problem myself without
your help."
L/9: "tell, how are you doing otherwise - I mean in meeting living expenses?"
L/3: "Just getting by. You know we live on a very modest - day to day basis.
